The Argument from Completeness of Causes
Sanusi presents the first argument for the world's eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first rational argument for the world's eternity, which is based on the completeness of causes and the impossibility of regress.

Core Idea
If all prerequisites existed eternally, the world must be eternal.

Sanusi begins by presenting the strongest philosophical argument for the eternity of the world: if everything necessary for the world's existence was already present in pre-eternity, then the world must have existed from eternity, because a complete cause cannot have a delayed effect. This argument forces a choice: either all prerequisites were present in pre-eternity or not, leading to an infinite regress. Let us examine this reasoning closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument passage
Read the Arabic passage containing the first proof. Notice the conditional structure: if all prerequisites exist in pre-eternity then the world exists; otherwise regress.
The argument is presented twice in the source; focus on the first occurrence.
2
Identify the key premise
The core premise is that an effect cannot be delayed from its complete cause (tam al-illa). Understand why this is considered axiomatic in kalam.
3
Trace the logical fork
The argument posits a fork: either all prerequisites exist in pre-eternity (leading to the world's eternity) or not (leading to regress). Both options purportedly force the world's eternity.
This is a classical dilemma.
4
Reflect on the force of the argument
Consider why this argument might be persuasive to those who deny the world's temporal origination. What assumptions does it rely on?
It assumes that the complete cause is fully present in pre-eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (تمسك القائلون) بقدم العالم بوجوه : الأول : أن جميع ما لا بد منه في وجود العالم إن كان حاصلاً في الأزل لزم وجوده، لامتناع التخلف عن تمام العلة، وإلا ننقل الكلام إلى ذلك الحادث فيتسلسل . والجواب : النقض بالحادث اليومي، وليس الفرق بأنه يستند الى حوادث فلكية متعاقبة لا إلى نهاية دفعاً له على أن الكلام في العالم الجسماني، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون حدوثه مشروطاً بتطورات أو إرادات . وبالجملة : حوادث متعاقبة لأمر مجرد. وقد سبق أن حديث لزوم المادة لكل حادث ضعيف، والمنع بأنه لم لا يجوز أن يكون من جملة مالا بد منه الإرادة التي من شأنها الترجيح أي وقت شاء من غير افتقار الى مرجح آخر، ويكون تعلق الإرادة أيضاً بمجرد الإرادة، ووجوب العالم بهذا التعليق لا ينافي اختيار الصانع بل يحققه . جميع الأول : أن ما لا بد منه لتأثير الصانع في العالم وإيجاده إياه، إما أن يكون حاصلا في الأزل أو لا . والثاني : باطل فتعين الأول وهو يستلزم المطلوب. وتقريره من وجهين: أحدهما: أنه لما وجد في الأزل جميع ما لا بد منه بوجود العالم لزم وجوده في الأزل، والمقدم حق فكذا التالي، أما اللزوم فلامتناع تخلف المعلول عن تمام علته لما مرّ، وأما حقية المقدم ، ولأنه لو لم يكن جميع ما لا بد منه لوجوده، إما أن يكون حاصلاً في الأزل أو لا ويتسلسل. هذا والجواب : النقض إجمالاً وتفصيلاً . أما إجمالاً فهو أنه لو صح الدليل لزم أن لا يكون ما يوجد اليوم من الحوادث حادثاً لجريانه فيه لا يقال الحادث اليومي يتوقف على استعدادات في المادة مستندة الى الحركات
He said: Those who claim the eternity of the world cling to aspects: The first: That all that is indispensable for the existence of the world – if it existed in pre-eternity, its existence would be necessary, because it is impossible for [the effect] to lag behind the complete cause; otherwise we transfer the discussion to that originated thing and there is regress. The answer: Refutation by the daily originated event – and the difference is not that it is based on successive celestial motions without end, in rejection of it, because the discussion is about the corporeal world; why may its origination not be conditioned by developments or wills? In summary: successive events for an abstract reason. Already mentioned is that the talk of matter being necessary for every originated thing is weak; and the prevention: why may it not be that among the indispensable things is the will, whose property is to give preference at any time it wills without needing another preponderator, and the attachment of the will is also by mere will, and the necessity of the world by this attachment does not contradict the Creator’s choice but rather confirms it. All of the first: That what is indispensable for the effect of the Maker in the world and His bringing it into existence – either it existed in pre-eternity or not. The second is false, so the first is determined, and it entails the required. Its exposition is from two aspects: One: When all that is indispensable for the existence of the world existed in pre-eternity, its existence in pre-eternity would be necessary; the premise is true, so the consequent. As for the entailment, it is because of the impossibility of the effect lagging behind its complete cause, as previously. As for the truth of the premise: because if not all that is indispensable for its existence existed, then either it existed in pre-eternity or not, and there is regress. This – and the answer: refutation in general and in detail. As for in general: That if the proof were valid, it would follow that what exists today of originated events would not be originated, because it applies to it. It cannot be said that the daily originated event depends on preparations in matter based on motions...
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage contains the first argument for the eternity of the world (qidam al-alam) and its refutation. The argument is presented as follows: All prerequisites (ma la budda minhu) for the existence of the world are either present in pre-eternity (azal) or not. If they are present in pre-eternity, then the world must exist from pre-eternity, because it is impossible for an effect to be delayed from its complete cause. If some prerequisites are not present in pre-eternity, then we transfer the discussion to that missing prerequisite; if it too is originated, we ask about its prerequisites, leading to an infinite regress. Thus the world must be eternal. The refutation (jawab) is given in both summary (ijmal) and detail (tafsil). The summary refutation points out that the same argument would apply to daily originated events (al-hadith al-yawmi), implying that they too would have to be eternal, which is false. The detail refutation introduces the will (irada) of the Creator as a factor that is not necessarily existing in pre-eternity in a way that forces the world into existence; rather, the will is a free choice that can attach at any time without needing an external preponderator. Thus the world's existence is contingent on the will, which is itself not part of the 'all that is indispensable' in the sense of a necessary condition that forces existence. The text then elaborates the argument again and reiterates the refutation, emphasizing that the argument fails because it overlooks the role of the Creator's will in determining the timing of creation.

Key Terms
قدم العالم
علة تامة
تخلف المعلول
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the argument is valid and proves the world's eternity definitively.
Correction: The argument assumes that all prerequisites must be simultaneously present in pre-eternity, but it overlooks the role of divine will which can specify the time of creation without requiring a new cause.

Checkpoint
What does the argument claim would happen if all prerequisites for the world were present in pre-eternity?
A) The world would not exist until a later time
B) The world would necessarily exist in pre-eternity
C) The world would come into existence gradually
D) An infinite regress would occur

Key Takeaway
The argument from completeness of causes attempts to prove the world's eternity by forcing a dilemma, but it assumes that all prerequisites are passive and does not accommodate divine will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that because all conditions were right, a result should have come immediately — only to be disappointed? How does this argument’s assumption that effect cannot be delayed from a complete cause challenge you to trust Allah’s timing over your own logic?
?
If the world were truly eternal, as this argument claims, what would that mean for your understanding of Allah’s sovereignty and your own purpose? Are you living as though this life is all that exists, or do you truly believe it was created for a reason?
?
The argument tries to prove eternity by eliminating the possibility of a delayed creation. But what if the delay itself is a sign of Allah’s wisdom? When you face delays in your own prayers or ambitions, do you see them as a deficiency in your prerequisites or as a call to deepen your reliance on Allah’s will?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
7 min
Refutation: Daily Events and Divine Will
Sanusi refutes the first argument using daily events and divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the first argument by pointing to daily originated events and by introducing the Creator's free will.

Core Idea
The same argument would make daily events eternal; God's will can delay without extra cause.

Having presented the argument for the world's eternity, Sanusi now provides a twofold refutation. First, he shows that the argument proves too much—it would also require that every daily event be eternal, which is absurd. Second, he invokes the divine will as a factor that can specify the time of existence without needing an external preponderator. This refutation preserves both the world's origination and God's free choice. Let's unpack these responses.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage containing the refutation. Note that it begins with 'Wa'l-jawab' and includes two main approaches: summary and detail.
The text uses 'ijmalan' and 'tafsilan'.
2
Understand the first refutation: the daily event
Sanusi argues that if the proof were sound, it would apply to any daily originated event, implying it too must be eternal. Since that is false, the argument is unsound.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Understand the second refutation: divine will
The detail refutation introduces the will (irada) of the Creator. This will can give preference to a moment without needing another preponderator. The world's existence becomes necessary only when the will attaches, not earlier.
This shows that the complete cause includes the will, which can choose the time.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this refutation upholds the world's temporality without compromising God's power. It also affirms that God's choice is not determined by external factors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (تمسك القائلون) بقدم العالم بوجوه : الأول : أن جميع ما لا بد منه في وجود العالم إن كان حاصلاً في الأزل لزم وجوده، لامتناع التخلف عن تمام العلة، وإلا ننقل الكلام إلى ذلك الحادث فيتسلسل . والجواب : النقض بالحادث اليومي، وليس الفرق بأنه يستند الى حوادث فلكية متعاقبة لا إلى نهاية دفعاً له على أن الكلام في العالم الجسماني، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون حدوثه مشروطاً بتطورات أو إرادات . وبالجملة : حوادث متعاقبة لأمر مجرد. وقد سبق أن حديث لزوم المادة لكل حادث ضعيف، والمنع بأنه لم لا يجوز أن يكون من جملة مالا بد منه الإرادة التي من شأنها الترجيح أي وقت شاء من غير افتقار الى مرجح آخر، ويكون تعلق الإرادة أيضاً بمجرد الإرادة، ووجوب العالم بهذا التعليق لا ينافي اختيار الصانع بل يحققه . جميع الأول : أن ما لا بد منه لتأثير الصانع في العالم وإيجاده إياه، إما أن يكون حاصلا في الأزل أو لا . والثاني : باطل فتعين الأول وهو يستلزم المطلوب. وتقريره من وجهين: أحدهما: أنه لما وجد في الأزل جميع ما لا بد منه بوجود العالم لزم وجوده في الأزل، والمقدم حق فكذا التالي، أما اللزوم فلامتناع تخلف المعلول عن تمام علته لما مرّ، وأما حقية المقدم ، ولأنه لو لم يكن جميع ما لا بد منه لوجوده، إما أن يكون حاصلاً في الأزل أو لا ويتسلسل. هذا والجواب : النقض إجمالاً وتفصيلاً . أما إجمالاً فهو أنه لو صح الدليل لزم أن لا يكون ما يوجد اليوم من الحوادث حادثاً لجريانه فيه لا يقال الحادث اليومي يتوقف على استعدادات في المادة مستندة الى الحركات

Commentary
This passage contains the first argument for the eternity of the world (qidam al-alam) and its refutation. The argument is presented as follows: All prerequisites (ma la budda minhu) for the existence of the world are either present in pre-eternity (azal) or not. If they are present in pre-eternity, then the world must exist from pre-eternity, because it is impossible for an effect to be delayed from its complete cause. If some prerequisites are not present in pre-eternity, then we transfer the discussion to that missing prerequisite; if it too is originated, we ask about its prerequisites, leading to an infinite regress. Thus the world must be eternal. The refutation (jawab) is given in both summary (ijmal) and detail (tafsil). The summary refutation points out that the same argument would apply to daily originated events (al-hadith al-yawmi), implying that they too would have to be eternal, which is false. The detail refutation introduces the will (irada) of the Creator as a factor that is not necessarily existing in pre-eternity in a way that forces the world into existence; rather, the will is a free choice that can attach at any time without needing an external preponderator. Thus the world's existence is contingent on the will, which is itself not part of the 'all that is indispensable' in the sense of a necessary condition that forces existence. The text then elaborates the argument again and reiterates the refutation, emphasizing that the argument fails because it overlooks the role of the Creator's will in determining the timing of creation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the refutation denies causality altogether.
Correction: Sanusi does not deny causality; he introduces a special cause—the divine will—that is not passive but active and free, breaking the necessity of simultaneousness.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the detailed refutation?
A) The world cannot be eternal because matter is needed
B) The argument would prove daily events are eternal
C) The will of the Creator can choose the time of creation without an additional preponderator
D) The world's existence is impossible

Key Takeaway
Sanusi refutes the eternity argument by showing it leads to absurd consequences and by affirming that God's free will can determine the moment of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's will being free and not bound by time, are there areas in your life where you have doubted His timing because you assumed He must act according to your schedule? Will you consciously surrender that timeline to Him today?
?
The refutation shows that our limited reasoning can lead to absurd conclusions if we impose temporal constraints on God. In what specific way have you tried to confine God's actions to your own understanding, and what step will you take to break that pattern?
?
If God's will alone is sufficient to determine the moment of creation, then your own existence and every event in your life is directly and freely willed by Him. How does this truth press you to live with deeper gratitude and trust, starting from this moment?
